==PAGE:3==
Summary
This thesis concerns multi-agent systems and agent programming related to the
Multi-Agent Programming Contest (MAPC). More speciﬁcally it concerns the
2015 MAPC scenario, namely the Agents in the city scenario.
The purpose of the project is to deﬁne and implement a prototype of a multi-
agent system using the agent programming language GOAL. The learning ob-
jectives are to understand the GOAL programming language, as well as the
scenario from the 2015 Multi-Agent Programming Contest.
The goal of the thesis is to create a working team in the 2015 MAPC. The team
is written in the GOAL programming language. GOAL is an agent programming
language for developing rational agents. The logic programming language Prolog
is used as the knowledge representation language in GOAL.

Preface
This thesis was prepared at DTU Compute in fulﬁlment of the requirements for
acquiring an M.Sc. in Engineering.
This project was conducted from August 24th 2015 to January 24th 2016 under
the supervision of Jørgen Villadsen. The thesis deals with multi-agent systems,
the GOAL agent programming language and the 2015 Multi-Agent Program-
ming Contest (MAPC).
The thesis consists of my analysis and implementation of the 2015 MAPC.
Lyngby, 24-January-2016

==PAGE:11==
Chapter 1
Introduction
A multi-agent system is a system with more than one intelligent agent in the
same environment.
The agents are able to sense and act.
Percepts provide
agents with information about the environment, so agents sense the environment
using percepts.
The Multi-Agent Programming Contest (MAPC) is an annual competition which
has been held every year since 2005. The aim of the MAPC is to stimulate re-
search in the area of multi-agent system development and programming, by
identifying key problems which require and enforce coordinated action. This
can help improve testing multi-agent programming languages.
The goal of the thesis is to make up a team of agents which could participate in
the Multi-Agent Programming Contest 2015, even though the team will not be
registered. The purpose of the project is to make the agents of the team behave
reasonably. By reasonably I mean move around and do something, preferably
beneﬁcial for the team.
The thesis starts with a theory about agents and multi-agent systems. This
is followed by an introduction to GOAL and GOAL programming. Then the
MAPC and the scenario is introduced. Thereafter the setup and percepts are
discussed. After that, an analysis and discussion of the project is made. Finally
the implementation is described.
==PAGE:12==
2
Introduction
==PAGE:13==
Chapter 2
Agents and multi-agent
systems
In this chapter agents and multi-agent systems are described and discussed.
2.1
Agents
Agents are entities which act in an environment. Agents perceive their environ-
ment, adapt to change, and create and pursue goals. Agents have intelligent
behavior, think humanly and rationally and act humanly and rationally. So
agents are entities that can perceive their environment through sensors and act
upon their environment through actuators.
Rational agents are the agents we are interested in.
Rationality is an ideal
performance measure so a rational agent is an agent that does the right thing,
given what he knows. A rational agent acts in order to achieve the best outcome.
Thus a rational agent behaves as well as possible. A rational agent chooses an
action that is expected to maximize its performance measure, given the percept
and knowledge the agent has. An performance measure in our case would be
to win all the matches. In order to do so we have to complete as many jobs as
quick as possible. Percept is a special kind of belief.
==PAGE:14==
4
Agents and multi-agent systems
2.2
Multi-agent systems
A multi-agent system is a system with more than one intelligent agent in the
same environment. It is a distributed system with intelligent agents that are
able to sense and act.
Percepts provide agents with information about the
environment, so agents sense the environment using percepts.[1]
==PAGE:15==
Chapter 3
The agent programming
language GOAL
In this chapter GOAL and GOAL programming are described and discussed.
3.1
GOAL
The GOAL language is a programming language for programming multi-agent
systems. The language was designed for the programming of autonomous decision-
making agents. GOAL is a rule-based language that supports reasoning about
the knowledge and the goals an agent pursues. GOAL is used for programming
rational agents. The agents derive their choice of action from their beliefs and
goals.
Agents may have multiple goals that specify what the agent wants to achieve at
a moment in the near or distant future. Goals specify a state of the environment
that an agent wants to establish, but not how to achieve such states. Agents
commit to their goals and drop them only when they have been achieved. So
agents are assumed to not have goals that they believe are already achieved.
Programming an agent means to program a strategy for action selection. Agents
==PAGE:16==
6
The agent programming language GOAL
use action rules to select actions, given their beliefs and goals. The type of
decision making in GOAL is based on human common sense decision making.
The decision making rules can be grouped together in modules. This allows
adding hierarchical structure to an agent program. This way agents can focus
their attention and put all their eﬀorts on achieving a subset of their goals, by
using a subset of their actions, and using only knowledge relevant to achieving
those goals.
Agents may communicate with each other to exchange information, and to co-
ordinate their actions. Agents communicate using the knowledge representation
language.
A GOAL agent program consists of six diﬀerent sections, including the knowl-
edge, beliefs, goals, a program section including action rules and action speciﬁ-
cation, and percept rules, respectively. Almost all sections are optional. Each
of these sections is represented in a knowledge representation language such as
Prolog.
Sections that deﬁne the agent’s initial knowledge, beliefs and goals should be
included in the init module. The beliefs of the agent represent the current state
whereas the goals of the agent represent the goal state. An agent may have
multiple goals at the same time. These goals may even conﬂict as each of the
goals may be realized at diﬀerent times.
Achievement goals are goals that the agent does not believe to be true. It is
also useful to be able to express that a goal has been achieved, which can be
done in GOAL.
An events module speciﬁes rules for processing percepts that are received from
the environment. We need to provide the agent with actions. GOAL is rule-
based and rules are structured into modules. The main module of a GOAL
agent speciﬁes a strategy for selecting actions by means of action rules.
Actions are speciﬁed using preconditions and postconditions. A precondition
speciﬁes when the action can be performed, i.e. is enabled. A postcondition
speciﬁes what the eﬀects of performing the action are. If the action needs to
be globally accessible, the action speciﬁcation needs to be included in the init
module.
==PAGE:17==
3.2 GOAL programming
7
3.2
GOAL programming
All agents are created as members of a multi-agent system (MAS). The ﬁrst
step in writing the agent is therefore creating a MAS. The MAS ﬁle references
an agent ﬁle (with extension .goal). A MAS ﬁle is used to set up a new MAS
project and to specify which agent ﬁles are needed for creating the multi-agent
system.
The extension .mas2g is used to indicate that the ﬁle is a MAS ﬁle. A MAS
ﬁle has to have at least two sections: An agent ﬁles section that tells the agent
platform which agent ﬁles it should use to create the MAS, and a launchpolicy
section that tells the platform when to create and launch an agent. Agent ﬁles
have to have the extension .goal. Agent ﬁles referenced in the launch policy
have to be listed in the agent ﬁles section.
In Figure 3.1 an example of an environment setup is shown, that is the .mas2g
ﬁle of the Blocks World MAS. An example of an agent ﬁle (.goal ﬁle) of the
Blocks World MAS can be seen in Figure 3.3 and is continued in Figure 3.4.
Figure 3.1: The MAS ﬁle (.mas2g ﬁle) for the Blocks World MAS
An environment can be added to a multi-agent system by adding an environment
section to the MAS ﬁle. We need to indicate where the environment we want to
use can be found. GOAL supports loading environments automatically if they
implement a well-deﬁned environment interface called EIS.
As Figure 3.2 shows, the structure of a GOAL program is transparent and easy
to understand. A knowledge representation language for GOAL, Prolog, tends
to result in very robust systems. When a Prolog code in GOAL does not work
==PAGE:18==
8
The agent programming language GOAL
Figure 3.2: The structure of an agent ﬁle (.goal ﬁle)
as intended, the agent is usually still able to make poor decisions, rather than
crash. In the competition this is not always positive since eﬃciency is important
for the agents to reach a decision before the deadline, and it is not good when
the agents perform actions that are not as expected.
We tell the agent it has a goal by putting it in a goals section. A goals section,
like a program section, has to be part of a module. If we are adding an initial
goal for the agent, we put the goals section into the init module of the agent.
The function of the init module is to initialize the agent before it starts making
decisions and performing actions. The goal in the goals section will be put into
the initial goal base of the agent.
We can also provide the agent with an initial belief. Instead of the goals section,
inside the init module, we use a beliefs section to add a belief to an agent’s
belief base. Beliefs should represent what is the case. An agent maintains two
databases of facts, the goal base consisting of things the agent wants to achieve,
==PAGE:19==
3.2 GOAL programming
9
and the belief base consisting of facts that the agent believes are true.
An agent is a set of modules. Modules like the init module are the basic compo-
nents an agent is made of. The init module initializes agents. In order to make
the agent do something we need other modules that allow the agent to make
decisions and perform actions. The most important module that an agent uses
to decide what to do next is called the main module.
An agent reacts to the event that it performed an action by calling a special
module called the event module. Every time that an agent performs an action it
will call this module. The event module’s main function is to update the agent’s
beliefs and goals after performing an action. Usually, performing an action will
change an agent’s environment and the beliefs of the agent should be updated
to reﬂect this.
A program section is used to add rules to a module. A bel operator is used to
inspect the current beliefs of the agent. The bel operator means that the agent
believes it. We tell the agent it can perform certain action by specifying it in
an actionspec section.
The knowledge representation language used is Prolog. In Prolog comma means
"and" and _ means "don’t care" and can be read as "something".
The information that an agent has about his environment consists of the knowl-
edge and the beliefs that the agent has. The main diﬀerence between knowledge
and beliefs in GOAL is that knowledge can not change at runtime and belief
can change at runtime. Rules in Prolog can not be changed, therefore it is good
to put them into the knowledge base.
Prolog supports the closed-world assumption.
The closed-world assumption
means that anything not known to be true is assumed to be false.
A goals
section that is part of the init module is used to create the initial goal base of
an agent. Any module can have a goals section.
Goals that need to be achieved at some future point in time are called achieve-
ment goals.
In contrast with achievement goals, maintenance goals without
deadlines should never be removed from an agent’s goal base. In order to achieve
a maintenance goal, an agent needs to perform actions, to ensure that this con-
dition does not change. Other types of goals are e.g. deadline goals that require
an agent to achieve a particular condition before some other condition becomes
true.
Atoms of the form goal(x) are used for inspecting what follows from the agent’s
goals. The condition x is a query speciﬁed in line with the rules of the knowledge
==PAGE:20==
10
The agent programming language GOAL
Figure 3.3: An agent ﬁle (stackBuilder.goal) for the Blocks World MAS (to
be continued)
representation language used. E.g. when using Prolog, x must be a valid Prolog
query.
Atoms can be negated using the not operator, i.e.
not(bel(x)) and
not(goal(x)).
In a section which has the goals separated by a comma, the goals represent a
single conjunctive goal which has to be achieved at the same time. On the other
hand if the goals are separated by a dot, they are individual goals that do not
have to be achieved at the same time. They can even be inconsistent.
An action speciﬁcation is used to capture the conditions that need to be true
to successfully execute an action and the conditions that will change in the
environment. In order to provide the agent with knowledge about the actions it
can perform, we need to write action speciﬁcations for all the actions that the
agent can perform to change the environment.
Each action that can be performed by an agent to change the environment needs
to be speciﬁed in the agent’s program. An agent needs to be informed about
environment actions in order to be able to understand when it can perform these
==PAGE:21==
3.2 GOAL programming
11
Figure 3.4: An agent ﬁle (stackBuilder.goal) continued for the Blocks World
MAS
actions and what the eﬀects of these actions are.
An action speciﬁcation speciﬁes the name of the action and its zero or more pa-
rameters, its precondition and postcondition. The precondition checks whether
the action can be performed and the postcondition speciﬁes that what has
changed after the action has been performed. Both the preconditions and post-
conditions consist of a conjunction of literals.
actionspec {
<actionname> (<parameters >) {
pre { <precondition > }
post { <postcondition > }
}
}
GOAL provides several built-in actions that do not need to be speciﬁed before
an agent can use them. These actions include the actions:
• print, which prints text to a console,
• insert, delete, which changes an agent’s beliefs,
• adopt, drop, which changes an agent’s goals, and
• log, which creates a log ﬁle.
==PAGE:22==
12
The agent programming language GOAL
An agent only drops a goal when it believes the goal has been achieved. One
issue with an agent that uses this strategy is that such an agent rather fanatically
commits to a goal. It would be more rational if an agent would also drop a goal
if he would believe that it is no longer possible to achieve the goal.
In order to select the right action, we need an action selection strategy that
performs a sequence of moves that transforms an initial state to the goal state.
So we need to design and implement a strategy for choosing the right actions
from an initial state to a goal state.
We have four diﬀerent styles of evaluating rules: linear, random, linearall and
randomall. The linear rule evaluation order means that the rules are evaluated
in linear order, from top to bottom. The random rule evaluation order selects a
rule at random until an applicable rule is found. Then that rule is applied. The
linearall order evaluates all rules that appear in a program section in the order
that they appear and applies all rules that are applicable. The randomall order
is similar to the linearall order but evaluates rules in random order.
After initializing the agent by means of an init module, the agent enters the
main decision cycle. In each decision cycle, ﬁrstly the event module is entered
and executed. The function of the event module is to handle events that are
received from an environment (e.g. percepts) or other agents (e.g. messages).
The idea is to make sure that the state of an agent is updated just before he
will decide which action to perform next. In each decision cycle, secondly the
main module is entered and executed. The purpose of the main module is to
execute the strategy of the agent for selecting actions in order to achieve the
agent’s goals. The agent will continue to execute the main decision cycle until
the agent is terminated.
A module can have the following sections:
knowledge: a set of deﬁnitions or rules, which represents the knowledge the
agent has about the environment. These deﬁnitions and rules are used to create
the knowledge base of the agent.
beliefs: a set of facts and rules called beliefs, which are typically used to rep-
resent an initial state of the environment. These beliefs are added to the belief
base of the agent.
goals: a set of goals, representing in what state the agent wants to be. These
goals are added to the goal base.
program: a set of action rules that deﬁne a strategy for action selection.
==PAGE:23==
3.2 GOAL programming
13
actionspec: a speciﬁcation of the preconditions and postconditions for each
environment or user-deﬁned action that the agent can perform. A precondition
speciﬁes when an action can be performed and a postcondition speciﬁes the
eﬀects of performing the action.
3.2.1
Environment
An agent connects to an entity in an environment by means of an environment
interface.
GOAL supports and requires the Environment Interface Standard
(EIS) to connect to an environment. EIS provides a toolbox for engineering
environment interfaces that has been developed to facilitate the connection and
interaction of agent platforms such as GOAL with environments.
A connection of an agent with an entity in an environment is established by
means of a MAS ﬁle. A MAS ﬁle is a ﬁle for launching a multi-agent system
including an environment and consists of three sections; environment section,
agentﬁles section and launchpolicy section.
An example of a MAS ﬁle can be seen in Figure 3.1. The environment section
is optional, and includes a reference to a jar ﬁle which enables GOAL to load
the interface to an environment. Agents are constructed from agent ﬁles (.goal
ﬁles) that have to be listed in the agentﬁles section. An agent is connected to
an entity with the help of a launch rule in the launchpolicy section. This launch
rule is triggered each time an entity is made available by the environment.
In order to process the percepts received from the environment, the event module
of the agent is executed. The processing of percepts is done by applying rules.
An event rule has the same form as any other rule, and is used to process events.
The literals percept(X) are used to inspect the percept base. These literals are
used in a combination with the bel operator. The second rule, in the list below,
is most often used when processing percepts.
We have three types of rules:
• if <condition> then <action>.
• forall <condition> do <action>.
• listall <Listvar> <- <condition> do <action>.
The main function of the main module is to specify an action selection strategy
for performing actions in the environment, whereas the main function of the
==PAGE:24==
14
The agent programming language GOAL
event module is to process events and update the agent’s knowledge, beliefs, and
goals accordingly. A second diﬀerence between main module and event module
is that, by default, all rules that occur in the event module are evaluated and
applied in order. So in the event module, each rule will be evaluated.
3.2.2
Communication between agents
In a multi-agent system where agents need to coordinate, it is useful for agents to
communicate about their beliefs and goals using messages. Processing messages
is similar to processing percepts. But there are some diﬀerences, for example
messages are not automatically removed whereas percepts are removed every
decision cycle.
Agents can exchange three diﬀerent types of messages. An agent can inform,
instruct, and ask something from another agent.
The right agent has to be
addressed when communicating.
Messages received are stored in an agent’s mailbox using the two keywords
sent(<recipient>, <message>) and received(<sender>, <message>) where <re-
cipient> indicates the agent or agents that receive the message, <sender> in-
dicates the sender agent, and <message> indicates the content of the message.
The content of a message has to be a valid expression in the knowledge repre-
sentation language that is used by the agents. When using Prolog, the content
of a message has to be a conjunction of literals.
The action <agentname>.send(<content>) is a built-in action to send <con-
tent> to an agent with a given <agentname>. <agentname> represents the
name of the agent as speciﬁed in the MAS ﬁle. An example is: “agent1.send(theFact)".
If an agent has received a <message> from a <sender> , then bel(received(<sender>,
<message>)) holds and the agent believes that he has received the message.
Similarly, bel(sent(<receiver>, <message>)) holds if an agent has sent a <mes-
sage> to a <receiver>.
It is important to delete a message right after having processed it, since mail-
boxes are not emptied automatically. Otherwise the same message would be
sent over and over again.
The three diﬀerent types of messages are:
==PAGE:25==
3.2 GOAL programming
15
• indicative message denoted by “:" and represents a fact
• declarative message denoted by “!" and represents a goal
• interogative message denoted by “?" and represents a question
The declarative message is represented by the keyword imp and the interogative
message is represented by the keyword int. The indicative message has no special
keyword since it is the default keyword.
==PAGE:26==
16
The agent programming language GOAL
==PAGE:27==
Chapter 4
The Multi-Agent
Programming Contest and
the scenario
In this chapter the MAPC and the scenario are described and discussed.
4.1
MAPC
The aim of the MAPC is to stimulate research in the area of multi-agent system
development and programming. It can help improve testing multi-agent pro-
gramming languages, platforms and tools. It can also help debugging existing
systems and to identify their weak and strong aspects. The MAPC is a contest
which has been held every year since 2005.
In each simulation step each agent receives a perception about the environment
and should respond by performing an action. The agent has to respond within
a given deadline.
==PAGE:28==
18
The Multi-Agent Programming Contest and the scenario
4.2
Scenario
The goal for the team of agents is to earn as much money as possible. Each
team consists of 4 agents, 1 car, 1 drone, 1 motorcycle, and 1 truck. So the
goal for each agent is to earn as much money as possible, which can be done
by completing as many jobs as possible, as well as collaborate with the other
agents in order to complete jobs. The agents have to work as a team, since each
kind of agent can only handle a subset of the tools, and the assembling of some
items require the collaboration of two or more agents. Money can be earned by
completing certain jobs, either priced jobs or auctioned.
Figure 4.1: A screenshot of a running simulation
Jobs can consist of buying, assembling and transporting items. Jobs can be
created by the environment and also by the teams.
There are ﬁve kinds of
facilities on the map: shop, storage, charging station, workshop, and dump
location.
==PAGE:29==
4.2 Scenario
19
The problem is that we need to get the team of agents up and running. We
need to connect to the EISMASSim environment.
One of the problems the
team comes across is when to choose auctioned jobs and when priced jobs.
Another problem is how the agents collaborate. The agents need to be able to
communicate in order to collaborate reasonably.
In the contest two teams compete in each match.
The agents move around
a map in a realistic city. We have four types of agents, i.e. four roles: cars,
drones, motorcycles and trucks.
The agents diﬀer in speed, how they move
around, battery capacity, the volume they can carry, i.e. their load capacity,
and which tools they can use to craft new items. Therefore the agents should
take these things into account when collaborating. They should decide which
agent does what part of the job, based on the qualities he has. For example, the
truck is the one of them who can carry the biggest things. So if the team needs
to carry very big things, or even many big things, they might consider using the
truck for that.
The team can bid on an auctioned job if they want to complete a particular
auctioned job. If the bid of that team is lower than the other team’s bid and
also higher than a certain threshold, then this team will be assigned the job.
If the team completes the auctioned job in time, it gets the bid amount as a
reward. On the other hand, if the team does not complete the auctioned job in
time, it will get ﬁned.
Priced jobs have a reward which is deﬁned initially. The reward is given to the
ﬁrst team to complete the job. So there is always a risk taking a priced job since
the team does not know whether or not it will complete the priced job faster
than the other team.
The teams have to decide which jobs to complete and how to do that. So the
teams should decide when to choose priced job and when auctioned. Also, the
team has to decide how to get the resources required to complete the job. The
agents need to take collaboration into account.
Items can be bought, assembled, given to a teammate, stored at a storage facility,
delivered as part of a job completion, recovered from a storage facility, and
dumped. When assembling an item the use of other items is required, some
which serve as prime matter and some which serve as tools.
Agents have a battery charge that gets decreased as they move around. They
need to make sure they never run out of battery charge, and should therefore
plan their visits to the charging station accordingly.
Several actions are available for the agents to choose from. These actions are:

Table 4.1: The four diﬀerent agent roles.
goto, buy, give, receive, store, retrieve, retrieve_delivered, dump, assemble,
assist_assemble, deliver_job, charge, bid_for_job, post_job, continue, skip,
and abort.
• The skip action is used to execute no action, or continue to execute an
ongoing action.
• The goto action is used to move the agent to a new location. A prerequisite
for the goto action is that the agent has to have enough battery charge
left.
• The charge action is used to charge the agent. The action is only available
at a charging station at the current location. The action may require many
steps until the agent is fully charged, even though there is no queue at the
charging station.
So it is important to execute the charge or continue
action in the later steps, if the agents wants to stay at the same place at
the charging station. Otherwise, it is placed at the end of the queue.
• The buy action is used to buy a speciﬁed number of a speciﬁed item. The
action is only available at a shop at the current location. The availability
==PAGE:31==
4.2 Scenario
21
and price may vary from shop to shop. A prerequisite is that the item is
available at the shop and the agent has to have enough free capacity to
receive the buying item.
• The give action is used to give a speciﬁed number of items to a teammate.
A prerequisite is that both agents have to be at the same location at the
same time, and the agents have to execute actions at the same time, i.e.
one of them executes the give action meanwhile the other executes the
receive action.
• The receive action is used to receive items from a teammate agent. The
prerequisite is that the agent has to have enough free capacity.
• The store action is used to store a number of items, paying a cost. The
action is only available at a storage location at the current location. The
items can be retrieved later by any agent from the same team. A prereq-
uisite is that enough free space is available at the storage.
• The retrieve action is used to retrieve a number of items, previously stored
by the team at a storage facility at this location.
The action is only
available at a storage location. A prerequisite is that the item is stored at
this storage location.
• The retrieve_delivered action is used to retrieve a number of items, previ-
ously delivered as part of a job’s completion. The action is only available
at a storage facility at the current location.
• The dump action is used to get rid of items the agent does not need and
to free the agents load. The action is only available at a dump facility at
the current location.
• The assemble action is used to assemble a single item and get hold of it.
The action creates a new item out of some prime matters and/or tools. The
agent has to hold the relevant prime matters and tools in order to be able
the assemble the item. The action is only available at a workshop. The
agent may be assisted by teammates that can contribute prime matters
and tools.
• The assist_assemble action is used to assist a teammate assembling an
item. The action is only available at a workshop.
• The deliver_job action is used to deliver items required to complete a
speciﬁed job. The action is only available at a speciﬁc storage facility at
the current location. Partial deliveries are also accepted.
• The bid_for_job action is used to bid for a speciﬁc auctioned job. The
job has to be in the auction period.
==PAGE:32==
22
The Multi-Agent Programming Contest and the scenario
• The post_job action is used to post a new job, that the other team may
choose to complete.
• The continue action is used to continue to execute an ongoing action,
either goto or charge. If there is no ongoing action, it does nothing. The
continue action is the same as the skip action.
• The abort action is used to cancel the execution of an ongoing action. The
action does nothing but stops an ongoing action if there is any.
The project can i.e. be useful preparation for creating multiple bots searching
websites. They can collaborate by each searching diﬀerent sites, and communi-
cate with the others about if, what was intended to ﬁnd, was found or not.
Agents communicate with the server by exchanging XML messages, i.e. XML
documents.

Chapter 5
Setup and percepts
In this chapter the setup of the environment and the percepts in the environment
are described and discussed.
5.1
Setup
The downloading of the MAPC Package is needed.
I installed version 7.79
of Java, version 7.2.3 of Prolog for Windows 64 bit, version 8071 of GOAL
(goal20140917v8071), Eclipse Mars for Windows 32 bit, and version 1.0.11 of
MSYS.
I followed the “Getting started with MAPC 2015” guide. After some trouble I
managed to pack the compiled ﬁle into a jar ﬁle and make the eismassim-2.3.jar
ﬁle. I used the command “jar cfvm eismassim-2.3.jar META-INF/MANIFEST.MF
* ”. So I did not use the command given in the guide as it did not work in my
case.
After the new package had been released (0.6.2) I followed the “Getting started
with MAPC 2015” guide again. But I made the following replacement (simi-
lar to what I did before): I compiled the following code in command prompt
==PAGE:36==
26
Setup and percepts
“jar cfvm eismassim-2.6.jar META-INF/MANIFEST.MF * ” while being in the
folder “C:/Users/Nanna/workspace/new env/bin”.
Following the guide (with
the above replacement) worked, so I got a “Hello World!” on the console and
was able to pack the code back into a jar ﬁle.
On the way I had trouble making everything work, since i.e. my Eclipse did not
work as supposed. I solved it by uninstalling Eclipse and installing it again, and
making some changes to the EnvironmentInterface.java among other things. My
java code worked after that (and has no errors). My goal code works as well
(and has no errors).
I have my own agents up and running now which I run directly from Eclipse
after having started the server and the map monitor. The agents run around
and execute actions properly.
In order to start the server and the map monitor and the agents, a few steps
have to be taken:
• Server: First a MSYS shell is opened and then is it needed to navigate to
the folder where the downloaded package is located. In my case, I typed
“cd C/Users/Nanna/massim-2015-0.6.2/massim/scripts/” and thereafter I
typed “./startServer.sh”. Then I typed “0”.
• Map monitor: After that I opened up another MSYS shell and typed
“cd C/Users/Nanna/massim-2015-0.6.2/massim/scripts/” and thereafter
I typed “./startMapMonitor.sh”.
• Agents: Finally a desired agent ﬁle is run, straight from Eclipse. After-
wards in order to start the simulation, the enter button has to be pressed
inside the server shell.
The java code is to get the environment up and running. I changed the ﬁle Envi-
ronmentInterface.java according to Nikolaj’s guide, and the ﬁle MANIFEST.MF
additionally. The Java ﬁles are the ﬁles I was required to include in order to
get the environment to work, according to Nikolaj’s guide. They are part of the
process of getting the environment up and running. I used App.java to test the
code. And I packed all the ﬁles back into a jar ﬁle (after making changes) and
that particular jar ﬁle is used in the GOAL code. The jar ﬁle has to be included
in the GOAL folder (same folder as the GOAL ﬁles) in Eclipse in order for the
GOAL ﬁles to work.
==PAGE:37==
5.2 Percepts
27
5.2
Percepts
Agents get percepts in each simulation step.
The server asks the agents to
perform an action and sends them corresponding percepts. The main purpose
of perceiving is to maintain an accurate representation of the environment. The
agents get knowledge about:
• the current simulation step
• their role, current charge and current load
• the team’s money
• the last action they made and the results from their last action
• their location and if they are inside a facility or not
• the length of their route
• the items they are holding and the amount
• the posted jobs by the team and taken jobs by the team (auctioned job
that has been won)
• other entities: their name, team, role and location
• facilities: their type, name, location, and other relevant information de-
pending on the type
• jobs: auctioned and priced, and relevant information depending on the
type
• products in the simulation: their name and volume, and how they can be
assembled (if the parameter list is empty, the product cannot be assem-
bled)
In each step of the simulation the server asks the agents to perform an action.
The server sends the agents the corresponding percepts. The percepts contain:
• the <perception> tag which has two attributes:
– deadline which is the latest moment in time when the server accepts
an action
– id which is the id that is supposed to be added to the action-message
==PAGE:38==
28
Setup and percepts
• the <simulation> tag which has one attribute:
– step which is the current simulation step
• the <self> tag which has twelve attributes:
– charge which is the current charge
– load which is the current load
– lastAction which is the last action performed
– lastActionParam which is the parameter of the last action per-
formed
– lastActionResult which is the result of the last action performed
– batteryCapacity which is the maximum charge
– loadCapacity which is the maximum load
– lat which is the latitude of the agent
– lon which is the longitude of the agent
– inFacility which is the facility where the agent is currently located
(or "none")
– fPosition which is the position in the facility above (or -1, if the
agent is not in a facility)
– routeLength which is the length of the route, if the agent is following
a route
• the <items> tag (included in the <self> tag) which contains the <item>
tag which has two attributes:
– name which is the name of the item an agent holds
– amount which is the amount of the item an agent holds
• the <route> tag (included in the <self> tag) which contains the <n> tag
which has three attributes:
– i which is the index in the ordered list of waypoints
– lat which is the latitude of the waypoint
– lon which is the longitude of the waypoint
• the <team> tag has the attribute money which is the current amount of
money that the team has.
The <team> tag has the tags <jobs-taken> and <jobs-posted>, which
can contain multiple <job> tags with the attribute id
• the <entities> tag which contains a <entity> tag for each agent with the
attributes name, team, lat, lon, role
==PAGE:39==
5.2 Percepts
29
• the <facilities> tag which contains one or more <chargingStation> tags,
one or more <dumpLocation> tags, one or more <shop> tags, one or more
<storage> tags, and one or more <workshop> tags with the following
attributes:
– the <chargingStation> tag has six attributes: name, lat, lon, rate
which is the charging rate, price, and slots which is the number
of charging outlets.
The <chargingStation> tag contains one tag
<info> which contains information only visible if the agent is nearby.
The <info> tag has the attribute qSize which represents the number
of vehicles waiting in line to charge
– the <dumpLocation> tag has four attributes: name, lat, lon, and
price
– the <shop> tag has three attributes: name, lat, lon, and has one
or more tag <item> with the attribute name, and the tag <info>
which has the three attributes cost, amount, restock. The <info>
tag contains information only visible if the agent is nearby
– the <storage> tag has six attributes: name, lat, lon, price, total-
Capacity, and usedCapacity, and has the tag <item> with the
three attributes: name, stored, and delivered.
– the <workshop> tag has four attributes: name, lat, lon, and price
• the <jobs> tag which contains one or more <auctionJob> tags and one
or more <pricedJob> tags with the following attributes:
– the <auctionJob> tag has six attributes: id, storage, begin, end,
ﬁne, and maxBid. The <auctioJob> tag also contains a tag <items>
which contains one or more tags <item> which have the attributes
name and amount
– the <pricedJob> tag has ﬁve attributes: id, storage, begin, end,
reward. The <pricedJob> tag also contains a tag <items> which
contains one or more tags <item> which have the attributes name,
amount, and delivered
Below a list of percepts can be found that can be available during a tournament:
• auctionJob(<Identiﬁer1>, <Identiﬁer2>, <Numeral3>, <Numeral4>, <Nu-
meral5>, <Numeral6>, [item(<Identiﬁer7>, <Identiﬁer8>), . . . ])
de-

id 2. storage 3. begin step 4. end step 5. ﬁne 6. maximum bid 7 item
name 8. amount

Each time just before an agent decides which action to perform, the agent pro-
cesses the percepts he receives.
The old percepts are removed and the new
percepts are inserted into the percept base of the agent. Additionally, the pro-
cessing of received percepts is needed which occurs in the event module.
The keyword percept is used to diﬀerentiate perceptual facts from other facts
in the knowledge or belief base. A percept received from the environment is
inserted into the percept base as the fact percept(. . . ).
==PAGE:43==
Chapter 6
Analysis and discussions
In this chapter the thesis project is analysed and discussed.
6.1
Analysis
The priority for each agent is to make sure it never runs out of charge. So the
agent has to make sure it can make it to the next charging station before running
out of charge. Therefore before choosing each action the agent calculates the
distance to the next charging station. And if the agent is running low on battery
charge and is not able to do anything else before going to the charging station,
then he goes to the charging station.
An agent should only give another agent an item if they are at the same location
or nearby, and the other agent needs that speciﬁc item the agent is holding. The
goto action might take several simulation steps to complete, depending on the
distance between the two agents and the speed of the agent which is moving
towards the other. Since the goto action might take time, it might be wiser to
assemble or buy the item instead, in the case where the agents are not at the
same location or near each other.
==PAGE:44==
34
Analysis and discussions
There are six ways to get hold of items; assemble them, buy them, receive them
from a teammate, retrieve them from a storage, retrieve delivered from storage,
and post a job where the job is to make the item.
One of the options is if
a teammate gives the item to you. The give and receive actions do not cost
anything so they should be used if both agents are at the same location. On the
other hand the agents have to be coordinated for that action to succeed, that
is they have to perform the actions give and receive at the same time. In order
to do so they have to communicate beforehand.
It might be a good idea for the agents to work in pairs. That way they might
perform better by working on two jobs at the same time. Since there are four
agents in each team, we have two pairs. This way the team can work on two
parts of the same job at the same time, or even two diﬀerent jobs. In order for
each pair to hold all the possible tools, we can pair the drone and truck together,
and then the car and motorcycle as well.
It should be taken into account that actions may fail, since actions fail randomly
with a 1 percent probability.
So it is important to check if the last action
performed was successful or not. If the action was not successful, that action
should be performed again until it becomes successful.
The main focus is on percepts since they give us knowledge about the environ-
ment. The same strategy is performed throughout the match. Each agent of
the four in the team is programmed in the same way.
According to my SWOT analysis, as can be seen in 6.1 and in a discussion
around the table, it is better to focus on priced jobs only. Also, posting jobs is
time consuming and optional so I will not implement that particular action.
I came up with several rules that I want to implement as part of my strategy.
• If agent is running out of charge then go to charging station.
• If job is available then do job.
• If a teammate needs help then help.
In order to develop successful agent, it is important to identify and take into
account the percepts that the agent receives from its environment, informing
the agent about the current state of the environment.
To start with or as soon as a job appears, agents should choose a job to complete.
They can choose one or more jobs at a certain time, although I would not
==PAGE:45==
6.1 Analysis
35
recommend that a single agent has more than one job at the same time. Agents
should choose job according to the items that are to be delivered and the tools
used. Preferably they choose jobs which contain some of the items they have or
can assemble. Also it might be good to take into account the distance to the
delivery storage if there are more than one job to choose from.
The structure for my team is that it chooses only priced jobs, not auctioned jobs.
If no agent holds the item/items to be delivered, then it should be assembled. If
an agent has little load capacity (less than 20) he should go to the nearest storage
and store some items in order to increase his load capacity. I am assuming that
the agent usually buys less than 20 units of the same item, preferably less than
10. The agents do not use the dump action since we want to use our items as
much as possible. Also, since it might cost us to dump, we rather want to store
our items instead of throwing them away.
Since all the agents can perform the same actions it is only needed to program
one agent which all the diﬀerent vehicles use. Depending on the vehicle the
agent has diﬀerent restrictions, e.g. speed, battery capacity, load capacity and
tools.
All agents of the team are programmed in the same way. But by knowing the
roles of everyone in the team the agents can behave accordingly. Relevant infor-
mation to send the team is your role, charge, load, lastAction, lastActionParam,
lastActionResult, lat, lon, inFacility, fPosition, items (both name and amount).
So each agent should message the others about some or all of this information.
Agents should inform their team about the items they hold. That way the team
has an overview about all the items the team has. Thus they can choose the
jobs accordingly. For example, if a team holds all items needed for a particular
job, it should choose that job over another.
Preferably an agent has to let his teammates know that he is working on a
speciﬁc item, i.e. delivering it to the speciﬁed place by either assembling it in
a workshop, buying it, receiving it from a teammate, or retrieving it from a
storage. This prevents two agents from working on the same item separately.
The buy action should be the last option. Agents should preferably assemble
the items at a workshop. When an agent is at the same location as a team agent
or nearby it should assist, if the other agent is assembling an item and needs
help. That way agents can complete jobs by collaborating.
When choosing which facility to go to, the nearest facility of the type wanted
should be chosen. So if the agent is going to a workshop he should go to the
nearest workshop. Wiser would be to go to a certain type of facility which is on
==PAGE:46==
36
Analysis and discussions
the way to where you are going next. For example if you are going to deliver
the job right after going to the workshop, the workshop should preferably be on
the way there.
The capacity should be calculated for both the battery and load, both maximum
capacity and what the agent has left. We need to know the maximum battery
capacity in order to know when an agent has full charge.
Also we need to
know the battery capacity the agent has left in order to know when to head to
the nearest charging station and charge. We need to know the maximum load
capacity in order to foresee a fully loaded agent. A fully loaded agent should be
avoided, by for example storing things at a storage location to free the agent’s
load. If the current load is the same as the maximum load, that speciﬁc agent
cannot get any more items unless he gets rid of some item or items by storing,
dumping or giving to a teammate. Also, if the current battery is less than 50
then the agent should go to the nearest charging station and charge.
Additionally, the distance from the agent to a location should be calculated.
From that knowledge we know which facility is nearest to the agent. The reason
why we would need to dump an item is if there is not enough space available in
the vehicle. And therefore calculating if we have enough space on the vehicle is
useful. To dump an item should be the last thing to do. Preferably we want to
store the item or use it, or if we cannot, we should give the item to a teammate
if an agent needs it or can use it and is nearby.
One of the most signiﬁcant challenges are to ﬁnd out how an agent knows that
he has arrived at a certain location he is moving to. And another challenge is
to ﬁnd out when an agent knows when he has a full charge when he is charging.
This knowledge can be acquired using percepts.
If an agent needs a prime matter and/or tool in order to assemble a job, he
should communicate it to the team. And if another agent has the prime matter
and/or the tool and is at the same location or nearby, he should help the agent.
If a tool is needed the nearest agent which holds the tool should come and help.
Agents should not cooperate unless they are near each other or preferably at the
same location. Meaning that an agent should not spend a lot of time moving
towards another agent in order to assist him. Moving takes time and then the
other agent might be waiting which is very unproductive. Instead the agent
might consider other actions depending on the circumstances.
For example
the agent could assemble the item or buy it or even retrieve it from a storage
location.
The three most important things to implement in my project, from the most
important to the least important are:
==PAGE:47==
6.2 Discussion
37
1. if charge is less than 50 then goto nearest chargingStation.
I chose 50
because it is 20 percent of 250 which is the battery capacity (maximum
charge) for the drone which has the least battery capacity. charge=current
charge
2. if priced job is available then do job
3. if loadCapacity - load < 20 then store an item or items at the nearest
storage location. I chose 20 because it is 20 percent of 100 which is the
load capacity (maximum load) for the drone which has the least load
capacity. loadCapacity=maximum load and load=current load. So if the
agent is almost fully loaded (the current load is nineteen items less than
the maximum load), the agent should go to a storage location and store
item or items he does not need
If one of the agents in the team holds a certain item which is needed to complete
the current job, he should tell the team about it. And afterwards he should
deliver the item to the speciﬁc storage location. In order to save time, if the
agent is far away from the delivery location he might consider meeting the drone
somewhere on the way and giving the item to the drone which can then deliver
it faster. That way other agents can focus on making the other items needed
for the current job or another job.
Similarly if an agent holds a prime matter which is needed for the completion
of the current job, he should inform the team. Then he can go to the nearest
workshop and assemble the item needed and thereafter deliver it to the speciﬁed
storage location. Also, if more than one prime matters are needed, some of which
the agent does not have, then another agent which has the needed prime matter
might consider helping if he is nearby.
6.2
Discussion
One of the most important things to think about is to make sure that the agents
do not run out of charge. When out of charge the agents can not do anything
productive. So the ﬁrst priority of each agent is to make sure he never runs out
of charge.
Another thing is that the agents need to take the shortest path from the initial
location to the arrival point.
Otherwise they spend time and charge doing
unproductive work.
==PAGE:48==
38
Analysis and discussions
One of the challenges in this project is for each agent to know that he has
completed an action. For example if an agent moves, he has to know that he
has moved and know his new location. The agents’ belief base and goal base
have to be updated every time an agent does an action.
One decision to make is when to choose priced job and when to choose auctioned.
An advantage of a priced job is that the team is not ﬁned if the other team
ﬁnishes the job before they do. A disadvantage of a priced job is that the other
team might be quicker to complete the job and thus get the price. But in that
case the team can retrieve the delivered items for later use. Retrieving delivered
items is possible for both priced and auctioned job and it has no cost associated.
If the other team is quicker to complete a certain priced job, the team could
store its partial delivery somewhere and get it back when a similar or even the
same job is available again. This is one example why I think it is better to
choose priced jobs over auctioned jobs.
An advantage of the auctioned job is that when the team has won the bid,
it does not need to compete with the other team about being the quickest to
complete the job. But the team still has to be quicker than a speciﬁc time limit.
A disadvantage of the auctioned job is that the bidding process takes time, and
the team might not even get the job if it bids too high or the other team bids
lower. So then the team wasted their precious time on something they did not
beneﬁt from. Another disadvantage is that if the team does not complete the
job in time it gets ﬁned.
In case of an auctioned job, it can be tricky to bid the relevant price. The team
does not want to get paid too little, but if their bid is too high they might not
get that particular job. Two reasons can be for not getting the auctioned job,
either the other team places a lower bid or the team’s bid is higher than the
threshold for the job. The threshold is not known to the team beforehand.
Type of job
Advantage
Disadvantage
Priced job
No bidding
The other team might be quicker
No ﬁne,
completing the job,
if not completed in time
thus winning the price
Auctioned job
No competing if bid is won
Bidding takes time
Fine if not completed in time
Can be tricky to bid the relevant price

if it bids too high or
the other team bids lower
Table 6.1: The advantages and disadvantages of the two diﬀerent types of jobs.
==PAGE:49==
Chapter 7
Implementation
In this chapter the implementation is described and discussed.
7.1
General
In my implementation I focused on the percepts since the percepts are the
agent’s way of sensing the environment. Sensing is important for acting in the
environment. An agent program uses the percepts and actions, and therefore it
can only be written after careful analysis of the percepts and actions that the
interface provides. So it is best to start developing an agent by writing percept
rules and action speciﬁcations for the agent.
One challenge I came across was ﬁnding out how an agent knows when he has
arrived at a certain location. For example when I moved an agent to a charging
station using the goto action, the agent kept executing the same action after
having arrived at the charging station. So it seemed that the agent did not know
that he was already at the charging station. By updating the percepts this can
be solved. The querying of the percepts base can be helpful to know when an
agent is inside a facility or not, for example by using the inFacility percept.
==PAGE:50==
40
Implementation
All of my agent ﬁles are identical, since the agents should behave in the same or
similar way. The only things that set the agents apart is their battery capacity,
load capacity, speed, routes (the way they move, either using roads or air), and
tools.
A lot of improvements can be made. For example the agents could message
each other a lot more. It would be good for everyone to know what everyone
else in the team is working on. So if one agent is done with his current task
then he could jump in and help someone else in the team who might need help.
Also, since time matters, some agent that moves faster than an other can help
another agent by moving some items for him.
7.2
The init module of the agent ﬁle
In the agent ﬁle (.goal ﬁle) I deﬁne several actions. Some of these actions are
the following:
• position(X): The agent X is located at the (lat, lon) position. The position
of X can be acquired from the percepts base
• isAt(X,_) : X is at something is deﬁned as the position of X
• holds(X,Y) : X holds Y is deﬁned as the agent X and the item Y are at
the same location
• agent(X): X is an agent is deﬁned as X is at something, so X is somewhere
in the map, and also X holds something
• item(Y): item can be prime matter or the product of one or more prime
matters. Item Y is deﬁned as an agent X holds it or not. The item can
both be at a location with an agent holding it or with no agent holding it.
• enoughSpace(me): X (me) has enough space if the load capacity (max-
imum load) minus the current load (already used space) is greater than
or equal to 20. I am assuming that each agent does not buy/receive/re-
trieve/retrive_delivered/assemble more than 20 items at a time.
• enoughCharge(me): X (me) has enough battery charge if the maximum
charge minus the current charge is greater than or equal to 50. I chose 50
since it is 20 percent of the battery capacity of the drone, which has the
lowest battery capacity.
==PAGE:51==
7.2 The init module of the agent ﬁle
41
• nearestFacility(Z): the facility Z is the nearest facility if Y and Z are
facilities of the same type, and for all Y’s the Y facility is further away
from me than Z, or as far away from me.
I also add preconditions and postconditions to some of the action speciﬁcation
actions. Some of them can be found below:
• goto(Z): the precondition is that I am not at Z and the postcondition is
that I am there
• charge: the precondition is that I am at a charging station
• buy(item, amount): the precondition is that I am at a shop, have enough
space, and do not hold the item. The postcondition is that I hold the item
and my load has increased by the amount I bought
• give(agent, item, amount): The precondition is that I hold the item and
am at the same location as the agent I am giving the item to. The post-
condition is that the agent holds the item, and I do not hold the item
• receive(item, amount): The precondition is that an agent Y holds the
item, me and Y are at the same location, I have enough space, and I do
not hold the item. The postcondition is that I hold the item and Y does
not hold the item
• store(item, amount): The precondition is that I am at a storage location
and am holding an item. The postcondition is that I do not hold the item
• retrieve(item, amount): The precondition is that I am at a storage loca-
tion, I have enough space, and I do not hold the item. A postcondition is
that I hold the item
• dump(item, amount): The precondition is that I am at a dump location
and I am holding the item. The postcondition is that I do not hold the
item
• assemble(item): The precondition is that I am at a workshop, I have
enough space, and I do not hold the item. The postcondition is that I am
holding the item.
• assist_assemble(agent): The precondition is that I am at a workshop, and
another agent is also at a workshop
• deliver_job(job): The precondition is that I am at a storage location
• bid_for_job(job, price): The precondition is that the type of the job has
to be an auctioned job
==PAGE:52==
42
Implementation
• skipInternal: This is an internal action that is not sent to the environment
and has no precondition and no postcondition
7.3
The main module of the agent ﬁle
In the main module I implemented the following rules:
• When the charging percentage reaches approximately 20 percent charge
(for the drone and less for the others), it is time for the agent to go to a
charging station and charge
• When the agent is at a charging station then he should charge
• When the agent has not enough space left he has to go to a storage and
store the item
• If there is an active priced job available, then the agent should assemble
items needed
• Right after assembling an item, the agent holds the item
• If an agent is alone at a workshop, he should assemble an item
• If, on the other hand, there is another agent in the workshop too, then
the later agent should assist the ﬁrst one.
• If the agent is at a storage location, then he should deliver job
• If the agent is at a storage location and does not have enough space, then
he should store a certain amount of an item
• If the agent is at a storage location and has enough space, then he should
retrieve a certain amount of an item
• If the agent is at a storage location and has enough space, then he should
retrieve a certain amount of a delivered item
• If the agent is at a shop, then he should buy a certain amount of items
• If the agent is at a dump location, then he should dump a certain amount
of items
• If no action could be found, then skip
==PAGE:53==
7.4 The event module of the agent ﬁle
43
7.4
The event module of the agent ﬁle
The event module is called every GOAL cycle and is used for handling percepts,
as well as updating the belief base and goal base of the agent before an action
is selected. In the event module I implemented the following:
• When a new step is detected, we should allow the program to process the
percepts, mails from other agents and choose a new action
• We should clear the stored percepts, synchronisation, and coordination
beliefs from the previous step
• When the agent receives a percept about simEnd (the end of the simula-
tion), then we should reset the agent’s belief base and also stop the agent
from sending actions
• If the percepts, mails, and coordination are not handled we should do so,
and make sure it does not happen again before the next step
• When the simStart (the start of the simulation) is percepted, but the agent
is not ready for a new match, then we quickly prepare for a new match by
resetting beliefs
• When the simStart is percepted and the agent is ready, then we should
handle the simStartPercepts and allow the program to send actions again
7.5
percepts.pl, knowledge.pl and agents.mod2g
In this section I describe the prolog ﬁles and module ﬁle in my GOAL imple-
mentation. The percepts.pl ﬁle consists of all the possible percepts which can
be acquired from the environment. The knowledge.pl ﬁle contains some knowl-
edge which is available to the agent. The agents.mod2g ﬁle contains additional
modules which are available to the agent and the agent uses in the agent ﬁle.
The three ﬁles in this section are imported in the init module of the agent ﬁle.
For more details on the code see Appendix B.
==PAGE:54==
44
Implementation
==PAGE:55==
Chapter 8
Conclusion
In this thesis project my goal was to create a working multi-agent system and
make improvements. I looked at HARDAC, a multi-agent system from 2012, and
used and improved some of their code. I also learned the GOAL programming
language and gained an understanding of the Multi-Agent Programming Contest
2015 scenario.
The thesis begins by describing and discussing agents and multi-agent systems.
Then the GOAL programming language is introduced and discussed, the lan-
guage that my agents are written in. I showed the syntax and the basic structure
of an agent ﬁle and multi-agent system’s ﬁle in GOAL.
I got the simulation up and running and ran matches. An analysis of the im-
plementation of the 2015 scenario has been made. The important details about
the implemented strategies have been explained. Additionally I discussed the
possibilities for future work.
It would be interesting to compare my solution to an identical multi-agent sys-
tem implemented in a diﬀerent programming language, in order to test whether
or not the GOAL language shows improved performance.

Conclusion
